  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5d038760-536f-4fcc-b97d-a3241e98fbd9'

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1688156705653502595">"I believe there is another man inside every man, a stranger..." writes Wilfred Leland James in the early pages of the riveting confession that makes up "1922." the first in this pitch-black quartet of mesmerizing tales from Stephen King. For James, that stranger is awakened when his wife, Arlette, proposes selling off the family homestead and moving to Omaha, setting in m</span>
  <span id="freeText1688156705653502595" style="display:none">"I believe there is another man inside every man, a stranger..." writes Wilfred Leland James in the early pages of the riveting confession that makes up "1922." the first in this pitch-black quartet of mesmerizing tales from Stephen King. For James, that stranger is awakened when his wife, Arlette, proposes selling off the family homestead and moving to Omaha, setting in motion a gruesome train of murder and madness.<br /><br /> In "Big Driver," a cozy-mystery writer named Tess encounters the stranger along a back road in Massachusetts when she takes a shortcut home after a book-club engagement. Violated and left for dead, Tess plots a revenge that will bring her face-to-face with another stranger: the one inside herself.<br /><br /> "Fair Extension," the shortest of these tales, is perhaps the nastiest and certainly the funniest. Making a deal with the devil not only saves Dave Streeter from a fatal cancer but provides rich recompense for a lifetime of resentment.<br /><br /> When her husband of more than twenty years is away on one of his business trips, Darcy Anderson looks for batteries in the garage. Her toe knocks up against a box under a worktable and she discovers the stranger inside her husband. It's a horrifying discovery, rendered with bristling intensity, and it definitely ends a good marriage.<br /><br /> Like Different Seasons and Four Past Midnight, which generated such enduring films as The Shawshank Redemption and Stand By Me, Full Dark, No Stars proves Stephen King a master of the long story form.<br />(front flap)<br /><br />Contains:<br />1922<br />Big Driver<br />A Fair Extension<br />A Good Marriage</span>
  <a data-text-id="1688156705653502595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_9678703').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_9678703').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });

        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/538970-i-m-considering-recommending-this-book-to">I&#39;m considering recommending this book to my book club, what are some good discussion questions I could submit along with it?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_538970'><a id="like_count_community_question_538970" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/538970?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F7912007-full-dark-no-stars">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/538970-i-m-considering-recommending-this-book-to">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/538970-i-m-considering-recommending-this-book-to">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/8790809-adam-ciotta"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/8790809-adam-ciotta">Adam Ciotta</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Most of these stories have an interesting level of verisimilitude due to the declining mental health of the protagonist. This brings up a lot of quest<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Most of these stories have an interesting level of verisimilitude due to the declining mental health of the protagonist. This brings up a lot of questions. <br /><br />For instance, discuss the implications of the epilogue of 1922. Were the rats ever real? Recall earlier scenes where they caused traumatic events that only Wilf witnessed. If the rats were just hallucinations what does the story suggest actually happened in those disturbing scenes? <br /><br />Due to the nature of these stories, the reader is encouraged to mistrust the narrator. When you read through this book again look for instances where you don't fully believe what the protagonist is telling you. That will definitely spark a lot of rewarding questions and discussion topics. <br /><br />I think this is a very good selection for a book club. I believe it is the most well structured book of short stories Stephen King has ever published and I hope you and your book club enjoy it!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_2669725191" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2669725191" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2669725191?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48328025-megs-bookrack?shelf=stephen-king-read">stephen-king-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2669725191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11684366093225183983"><i>Full Dark, No Stars</i> is as harrowing and horrifying as it gets.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450941558ra/17489990.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>For many years, King's <i>Different Seasons</i> claimed the title of my <b>#1 favorite, short-story collection</b>. <br/><br/>Well, you heard it hear first, folks: <u>times, they are a changing!</u><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503985972ra/23713087.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>That honor now goes to this <b>delightfully dark collection</b> that tells four tales of ordinary people placed into extraordinary, and gut-churning, circumstances. <br/><br/>The novellas within <i>Full Dark, No Stars</i> each examine the deepest, darkest corners of the human mind.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547838278ra/26937666.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>My ratings fo</span>
  <span id="freeText11684366093225183983" style="display:none"><i>Full Dark, No Stars</i> is as harrowing and horrifying as it gets.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450941558ra/17489990.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For many years, King's <i>Different Seasons</i> claimed the title of my <b>#1 favorite, short-story collection</b>. <br><br>Well, you heard it hear first, folks: <u>times, they are a changing!</u><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503985972ra/23713087.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That honor now goes to this <b>delightfully dark collection</b> that tells four tales of ordinary people placed into extraordinary, and gut-churning, circumstances. <br><br>The novellas within <i>Full Dark, No Stars</i> each examine the deepest, darkest corners of the human mind.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547838278ra/26937666.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My ratings for each of the stories are as follows:<br><br><u>1922</u>: 5-stars<br><u>Big Driver</u>: 5-stars<br><u>Fair Extension</u>: 5-stars<br><u>A Good Marriage</u>: 4.5-stars<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510002243ra/24378025.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was pulled deep into every story, until the entire atmosphere engulfed me. <br><br>The characters, as always with King, were so believably written. Their thoughts were relatable and although grim, peppered with classic King humor. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513088743ra/24661481.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I cannot believe that I waited this long to read this collection. It's certain to be the first reading of many. <br><br>I love to reread King books, as I always notice new things with rereads. Overall, I felt this was absolutely superb! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597591173ra/29976287.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you can do gruesome and chilling, this is for you. Pick it up and be ready to be petrified by the worst monsters of all: mankind.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547838279ra/26937667.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_2094911907" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2094911907" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2094911907?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781444712544" href="/book/show/7877206-full-dark-no-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50893023-johann-jobis89?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2094911907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11477159088418300666">"Life is fair. We all get the same nine-month shake in the box, and then the dice roll. Some people get a run of sevens. Some people, unfortunately, get snake-eyes. It's just how the world is."<br/><br/>Full Dark, No Stars is a collection of 4 novellas in which King explores the "dark side" to people, and how exactly would you react if placed in certain situations? For example, what would you do if you found out that your husband of over 20 years has been hiding a dark secret? How would you react if a a p</span>
  <span id="freeText11477159088418300666" style="display:none">"Life is fair. We all get the same nine-month shake in the box, and then the dice roll. Some people get a run of sevens. Some people, unfortunately, get snake-eyes. It's just how the world is."<br /><br />Full Dark, No Stars is a collection of 4 novellas in which King explores the "dark side" to people, and how exactly would you react if placed in certain situations? For example, what would you do if you found out that your husband of over 20 years has been hiding a dark secret? How would you react if a a psychopath raped you and left you for dead? If given the opportunity to pass your hardships onto someone else... would you?<br /><br />One of my favourite aspects, and one of the most horrifying things, about this collection is that some of these scenarios could actually happen. You could very easily find yourself in a situation where you don't know your spouse as well as you thought you did. And there is definitely the potential to encounter brutal rapists/murderers whilst driving down quiet backroads. Although there is a slight supernatural element to 1922, there is still the very real possibility of making one single bad decision that will continue to impact and haunt you for years. Even the story Fair Extension makes you question how far you are willing to go to save your own ass at the detriment of someone else.<br /><br />1922 was a great opener for the collection, it was scary, hard-hitting, and sucks you into the story very quickly. One of the best short stories (or novellas, whatever) that I've ever read from King. It was brilliant! Next up was Big Driver, which was hard to read at times; it was brutal, visceral and terrifying, especially reading this as a woman. I can't deny that I have recently felt uneasy driving down the backroads around my house...maybe stick to main busy roads in future! Fair Extension was awesome, I loved how King juxtaposed the fate of the two families. I'd read an entire book based on that story and idea. Lastly, A Good Marriage. This was one I felt slightly less excited about reading about as I had already watched the adaptation last year and just thought it was okay. But I REALLY enjoyed this one - Darcy is a badass. I can't even begin to imagine what I would do in that scenario.<br /><br />It's very easy to see where the title for this collection comes from - these are dark, heavy stories, with pretty much no light or positive outcomes. I thoroughly enjoyed each story and would probably give each individual novella five stars, which is very rare when it comes to collections of short stories or novellas. I can honestly say I was sad to come to the end of this collection and I think I now have a new book to recommend to people who are looking to venture into the world of King. Highly recommend this one!!<br /><br />King, I missed you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11477159088418300666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_128825077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128825077" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128825077?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=uncle-stevie">uncle-stevie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128825077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17409202788764073978">There’s a fair amount of criticism out there about Stephen King. A lot of it is valid, but there are certain times that he’s the perfect author to be reading. Like last night when a winter storm blew through. Freezing temperatures, snow, ice, and high winds made it look like an Artic wasteland outside. As I lay reading under my warm blankets, I paused for a moment and listened to the wind making the house creak and the sleet hitting the windows, and thought, “This is just about the perfect setti</span>
  <span id="freeText17409202788764073978" style="display:none">There’s a fair amount of criticism out there about Stephen King. A lot of it is valid, but there are certain times that he’s the perfect author to be reading. Like last night when a winter storm blew through. Freezing temperatures, snow, ice, and high winds made it look like an Artic wasteland outside. As I lay reading under my warm blankets, I paused for a moment and listened to the wind making the house creak and the sleet hitting the windows, and thought, “This is just about the perfect setting to be reading a Stephen King book.” The fact that it was a very damn good Stephen King book was an excellent bonus.<br /><br />As if to give us a break after recent high page count books like <i>Under the Dome</i> and <i>Duma Key</i>, King delivers four short-n-sweet novellas focusing on the nastier sides of people with just a hint of the supernatural. These are four tales about the lives we build that we tell ourselves our safe, sane and secure, but there’s always darkness lurking at the edges. King points out that sometimes we’re the ones who invite that darkness in.<br /><br />In <i>1922</i>, a Depression-era farmer in the Midwest just wants to work with his son and read books in the evening, but his wife wants to sell some land her father left her to a hog factory and use the money to move to the city. When the two can’t reach an agreement, the farmer decides to murder her and hide the body in an old well. Even worse, he manipulates his son into helping. What results is a chilling story of the unintended consequences that one crime and the ensuing guilt can cause.<br /><br /><i>Big Driver</i> features Tess, an author who writes cozy mysteries about a group of elderly amateur female detectives that are popular with grandma-types. Taking a short cut home from a speaking/signing engagement, a flat tire leads to Tess being raped and left for dead. After escaping, Tess realizes that since she’s a quasi-celebrity going to the police would result in a media firestorm that would taint the rest of her life so she decides to seek her own revenge.<br /><br />Dave Streeter is a man with terminal cancer who gets a mysterious offer for fifteen more healthy years of life in <i>Fair Extension</i>, but he has to nominate someone to get a heaping dose of bad luck in his place. Since he’s got a lot of resentment and grudges against his best friend Tom and his perfect life, Streeter decides that his old buddy deserves some misfortune.<br /><br />The question in <i>A Good Marriage</i> is how well do you know your spouse? Darcy and Bob have been together 25 years and if things are a bit dull and ordinary at this point, they’ve built a good life and are generally content. When Bob’s away on business, Darcy goes looking for batteries in the garage and discovers a horrifying secret that her husband has been keeping.<br /><br />This is some of the best stuff that King has done in years. By focusing on human nature rather than supernatural monsters, he was able to create some very relatable yet scary stories. We know that we won’t really be trapped in old hotels filled with ghosts or live in a town overrun by vampires or chased by demon cars that drive themselves. But getting a flat tire on a lonely road? Finding a dark secret about a spouse? Being jealous of a friend doing better than yourself? Watching your life unravel because of a bad decision you’ve tried to hide? Those are things that we really fear, and King uses them all skillfully to deliver some of his creepiest stories yet.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17409202788764073978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1271588426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1271588426" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1271588426?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1271588426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9112298567799386361"><b>1922:</b> A man coerces his son into helping him murder his wife. Can they keep their sanity in the aftermath?<br/><br/>1922 is a latter day retelling of A Telltale Heart, only with rats and a Bonnie and Clyde side-story. It's also damn good and a prime example of what Stephen King can do when he has a limited number of pages to work with instead of the entire paper output of a redwood forest.<br/><br/><b>Big Driver:</b> After taking a shortcut down an unfamiliar road, a writer is raped and left in a culvert to die but her at</span>
  <span id="freeText9112298567799386361" style="display:none"><b>1922:</b> A man coerces his son into helping him murder his wife. Can they keep their sanity in the aftermath?<br /><br />1922 is a latter day retelling of A Telltale Heart, only with rats and a Bonnie and Clyde side-story. It's also damn good and a prime example of what Stephen King can do when he has a limited number of pages to work with instead of the entire paper output of a redwood forest.<br /><br /><b>Big Driver:</b> After taking a shortcut down an unfamiliar road, a writer is raped and left in a culvert to die but her attacker made a mistake. He let her live...<br /><br />Wow, this was a powerful, dark, unsettling tale of rape and revenge. Did I mention it was uncomfortable? A woman getting raped is much more horrifying than a nightmare clown lurking in the sewers. I kept having revenge fantasies of my own on behalf of the women in my life while reading this.<br /><br /><b>Fair Extension:</b> When a mysterious stranger offers Harry Streeter 15-20 more years of life, he jumps at the chance. But with deals of this kind, there's always a catch...<br /><br />This one kind of reminds me of The Monkey's Paw. For all the good luck the Streeter family has, shit rains down upon the man Streeter hates the most.<br /><br /><b>A Good Marriage:</b> Darcy Anderson thought she had a good marriage until she found something her husband hid in their garage...<br /><br />The point this story drives home is how little anyone really knows anyone else. Chilling and very effective.<br /><br />Full Dark, No Stars isn't my favorite King book but it's chock full of Kingliness and is an excellent example of what sai King can do when he isn't allowed to write phonebook sized tomes. Four out of five stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9112298567799386361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2272837935" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2272837935" />
    <a title="Sr3yas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23097409-sr3yas"><img alt="Sr3yas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520526764p2/23097409.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2272837935?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sr3yas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sr3yas" href="/user/show/23097409-sr3yas">Sr3yas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9307151-full-dark-no-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2272837935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6644654699816188763"><i>
  <b>Full Dark, Four Stars. </b>
</i><br/><br/>In Full Dark, No Stars, we get four dark tales filled with murder, revenge, terror, and death. That, my friend, is regular Monday morning at Stephen King's head anyway! <br/><br/><u>
  <b><i>Novella #1</i> 1922</b>
</u><br/>To be honest, I picked up Full Dark, No Stars after watching the trailer for 1922 movie adaptation, and I am happy to say that the novella delivers. The story is set in Nebraska and the year is <i>(that's right, you guessed it)</i> 1922. We are introduced to <i>Wilfred James</i>, a farmer who loves</span>
  <span id="freeText6644654699816188763" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Full Dark, Four Stars. </b>
</i><br><br>In Full Dark, No Stars, we get four dark tales filled with murder, revenge, terror, and death. That, my friend, is regular Monday morning at Stephen King's head anyway! <br><br><u>
  <b><i>Novella #1</i> 1922</b>
</u><br>To be honest, I picked up Full Dark, No Stars after watching the trailer for 1922 movie adaptation, and I am happy to say that the novella delivers. The story is set in Nebraska and the year is <i>(that's right, you guessed it)</i> 1922. We are introduced to <i>Wilfred James</i>, a farmer who loves his way of living, and his wife, <i>Arlette,</i> who despise their way of living, and their teenage son, <i>Henry.</i> The story takes a dark turn when Arlette decides to sell the land she inherited from her father and move to the city, a decision James can't even consider. You see, he is kind of person who loves the land he lives in, and he wants to start farming in Arlette's land too.<br><br>I think you can see where this is going.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516977286i/24937043.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What you will not see if you don't read this book is <i>how good the narration is</i>. The story is narrated by James, and King did an excellent job fleshing out the characters and the incidents. I loved the period drama King brought to the story. The locations, the mentality of people, the creeping horror, and bloody good storytelling makes this the best story in this collection for me.<br><br><u>
  <b><i>Novella #2</i> Big Driver</b>
</u> <br><br>In king's Short story collection book called <i>Everything's Eventual</i>, there was story named <i>In the Deathroom.</i> In author's note, King hinted that <i>In the Deathroom</i> is basically a wish fulfillment where the protagonist pulls through even though the cards were stacked against him.<br><br>Big Driver felt like <i>In the Death room,</i> but of course, Big Driver is longer and digs deep into its characters. Yet, I felt like the story was a bit unreal at times. The story is hard to read because it involves <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[rape and assault  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and towards the end, it felt a little bit too neat. <br><br>Well, this is not by any means a bad story, nevertheless, Big Driver is my least favorite story in this collection. <br><br><u>
  <b><i>Novella #3</i> Fair Extension</b>
</u><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>❝Everyone wants an extension, Mr. Streeter. If you were a young woman with a love of shopping, I’d offer you a credit extension. If you were a man with a small penis—genetics can be so cruel—I’d offer you a dick extension.Short men frequently want a height extension. If you did want more hair, Mr. Streeter, I’d be happy to sell you a hair extension.❞</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516977286i/24937044._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The dude under that yellow umbrella sells extensions. Dave Streeter is dying because of cancer. And I can smell a trade coming up. But What will be the price?<br><br>This is a very short novella. Incidentally, it is the most fucked up novella too, especially the second half! All I can say is read and find out!<br><br><u>
  <b><i>Novella #4</i> Good Marriage</b>
</u><br><br>You know what? I am not getting married, period. This right here is some scary shit. Once again, we find that true horror comes from humans, and not ghosts. <br><br>It all starts when Darcy stumbles upon a box in the garage. Oh, Wait. Darcy is happily married to Bob for 27 years. They really love each other. But do they really know each other? <br><br>Ok. back to the box!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1516977286ra/24937045.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I shouldn't tell you, but it's not a head. But it's pretty terrible.<br><br>I really enjoyed the story. The characters and the inner monologues of Darcy were really well written. The antagonist of this story is a fine example of King's ability to create screwed up characters! <br><br><b>
  <u>Parting thoughts:</u>
</b><br>Full Dark, No Stars is a solid collection of four stories which delves deep into the darkness of human mind and how seamlessly ordinary people will react in extraordinary situations. Take heed, be prepared, and when stars around you go out and darkness engulf the flawless landscape around you, you'll finally understand what sort of person you are. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516977286i/24937046.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6644654699816188763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Neil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1239026-neil"><img alt="Neil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484358p2/1239026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129529471?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil" href="/user/show/1239026-neil">Neil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer129529471&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129529471" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15266297674772664442">I reviewed it in the Guardian - you can read the full review over at <a href='http://www.guardian.co.uk/books/2010/nov/05/full-dark-stephen-king-review' rel='nofollow noopener'>http://www.guardian.co.uk/books/2010/nov/05/full-dark-stephen-king-review</a>, so I'm not going to put it all up here for a while. But it begins...<br/><br/><b> Novellas are an odd form of writing, and there is no love for them in publishing. They are the wrong size. You need about four of them to make a standard-sized book.<br/><br/>It has been almost 30 years since Stephen King's first set of four novellas, Different Seasons, four stories written in th</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15266297674772664442" style="display:none">I reviewed it in the Guardian - you can read the full review over at <a href="http://www.guardian.co.uk/books/2010/nov/05/full-dark-stephen-king-review" rel="nofollow noopener">http://www.guardian.co.uk/books/2010/nov/05/full-dark-stephen-king-review</a>, so I'm not going to put it all up here for a while. But it begins...<br /><br /><b> Novellas are an odd form of writing, and there is no love for them in publishing. They are the wrong size. You need about four of them to make a standard-sized book.<br /><br />It has been almost 30 years since Stephen King's first set of four novellas, Different Seasons, four stories written in the golden dawn of his career. They were mostly fantasy-free, and three of them were filmed (as Stand By Me, The Shawshank Redemption and Apt Pupil). They were sharp, smart, dark stories of a perfect length to film – longer than the short stories King had written for men's magazines early in his career, shorter than the blockbuster novels he had started to carve out, following the success of Carrie (which was itself a novella, padded out to novel-length with commentary on the events of the book). </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15266297674772664442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3451417187" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22727329-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467838647p2/22727329.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3451417187?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/22727329-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3451417187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17409594436974755139">I may have stepped too far into the King waters this time, I should probably stick closer to shore. And I <b>really</b> should have taken the title at face value.<br/><br/>This collection was intense and disturbing exploring the darkest underbelly of human behavior. I’d also like to add that they’re not easy to forget, they have inhabited a part of my brain and I’d really like them to leave. Please.<br/><br/><b>Big Driver</b> - Brutal and unsettling. A violent rape and its aftermath. A cozy writer finds her inner warrior. There </span>
  <span id="freeText17409594436974755139" style="display:none">I may have stepped too far into the King waters this time, I should probably stick closer to shore. And I <b>really</b> should have taken the title at face value.<br /><br />This collection was intense and disturbing exploring the darkest underbelly of human behavior. I’d also like to add that they’re not easy to forget, they have inhabited a part of my brain and I’d really like them to leave. Please.<br /><br /><b>Big Driver</b> - Brutal and unsettling. A violent rape and its aftermath. A cozy writer finds her inner warrior. There were moments when I was reading this novella when I forgot to breathe.<br /><br /><b>Fair Extension</b> - Deal with the devil story that explores that most dark of emotions, envy. There’s a reason it’s one of the seven deadly sins. Sans violence, gore or things that go bump in the night, this one was the nastiest for me and I wanted to scrub my soul with bleach.<br /><br /><b>A Good Marriage</b> - Unnerving and the best of the four. I previously read this as a standalone, not knowing that it was part of this collection. Mr. King asks the question, is it possible to really know someone?<br /><br /><b>1922</b> - A horror show and too much for this squeamish gal. True King fans (which I’ll never be due to being a wuss) think this is the best of the lot. If I’d finished reading it, I would likely not get any more sleep and I need my beauty rest.<br /><br />So why am I still rating this with four stars? Horrifying as the stories may be, dang if he didn’t pull me under and make me consider what horrible people might do. Now, anyone know of a good lobotomist? </span>
  <a data-text-id="17409594436974755139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1332658956" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1332658956" />
    <a title="Ron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43881851-ron"><img alt="Ron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557265090p2/43881851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1332658956?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ron" href="/user/show/43881851-ron">Ron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=anthology-collection">anthology-collection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=novella">novella</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1332658956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5909247549234633853">I finished!<br/><br/>Full Dark, No Stars. I always liked that title. It’s a subtle warning for what lies ahead within these four novellas, but I didn’t realize how accurate it was, until I read them all. Let me add a warning you before you decide to read them: <u>Not for the faint of heart</u>. <br/><br/><b>
  <u>Big Driver</u>
</b><br/>Tess is a mystery writer, and like writers do, she attends a few speaking engagements throughout the year. Get close to her fans, talk about her latest book, and sign some autographs. She only has a couple o</span>
  <span id="freeText5909247549234633853" style="display:none">I finished!<br /><br />Full Dark, No Stars. I always liked that title. It’s a subtle warning for what lies ahead within these four novellas, but I didn’t realize how accurate it was, until I read them all. Let me add a warning you before you decide to read them: <u>Not for the faint of heart</u>. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Big Driver</u>
</b><br />Tess is a mystery writer, and like writers do, she attends a few speaking engagements throughout the year. Get close to her fans, talk about her latest book, and sign some autographs. She only has a couple of rules, and one is “keep it close to home” - within a day’s driving distance. So when a lady calls about a last minute fill-in, just 60 miles down the road in Chicopee, she says yes. “Easy-as-can-beezy”. (I don’t know about you, but that saying gets stuck on the middle of my tongue).<br />And everything is easy-as… well you know, until Tess takes a short-cut home, one offered up by that nice librarian in Chicopee, and a nice day turns into the most frightening of days for a woman stranded. Like 1922, this novella gets scary in a hurry, not in the “typical” horror sense, but in an all too real way. The worst part of this story was the ugliness of man. The best part was the misdirection. I thought it would go one way. It went another. And for the most part, I cheered those choices. For added dialogue in a mainly singular character novel, Tess talks to (and hears from) her cat, and also her TomTom - strangely good.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Fair Extension</u>
</b><br />“Sold his soul to the devil”, or so the old saying goes. Just a fair extension of time for a man dying. Except there is always a price to pay, but the twist is that another will foot this bill. To me, this was the darkest of these four stories. Reads like a parody, which it has to be because – wow - the satire of mean spiritedness is steeped in exaggeration. That was tough for me to overcome.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>A Good Marriage</u>
</b><br />Of course when you see the title, A Good Marriage, you know that it will be anything but. And, you’d be right. I really wish I hadn’t known the synopsis before reading this time around. I read this one upon its initial release, and even though most of that memory has faded with time, I did not forget the biggest piece of the puzzle. I’d like to go back to experience the moment Darcy discovers her husband secret, hidden beneath the garage workbench. It’s a crazy secret. So go into this one blind, if you can. The ending is really good. I guess within these stories there shines a little light after all. Like King says in the afterword, “the people in these stories are not without hope.”<br /><br /><b>
  <u>1922 – (review first posted on 11/19/17)</u>
</b><br />If you happen to come across a well in a Stephen King novel, you can bet dollars to donuts that something’s going in it. Notice I didn’t get specific as to what that thing is, but I am sure there are some immediate and close guesses for those who know King. What’s different about this one? She’s a shocker in the get-go.<br /><br />Here’s a conversation I had with my mom the other night. She knows how much I like Stephen King:<br />“Oh gosh, I watched that movie 1922 on Netflix last night!”, she says. (Note: By her tone, I knew a rave review was not forthcoming.)<br />“Uh-oh”, I said. “Bloody?” (me knowing full well that it probably was that **snicker-snicker**, but at this point I had not read the novella, or watched the movie).<br /><b>”O-M-G!”</b>, mom said. (you’d really have to see her face for full dramatic effect – much disgust) “I about turned it off a few times! But, I ended up watching all of it.”<br /><br />What did I hear in all of that? She watched all of it. Hee-hee.<br /><br />So of course I picked up the novella the next day and began my reading. OMG indeed Ma. She was right. The beginning of this story is one bitter pill to swallow. It is raw, and it is ugly. If the movie is anything like the book, then egad. I’m going to say that it’s not for everyone. That’s too bad too, because if you can get past that beginning, this one settles down (excepting them darned rats) into a surprisingly melancholy story of a man looking back in regret. He may not regret the act, but certainly does regret the aftermath, a whirlwind that will destroy more than one future.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>”Do you like how things turned out, Wilf? Was it worth it?”</i>
</blockquote><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5909247549234633853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_129993095" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129993095" />
    <a title="Lou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3699303-lou"><img alt="Lou" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312212794p2/3699303.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129993095?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lou" href="/user/show/3699303-lou">Lou</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129993095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17737402759439999023"><b>
  <u>Best of 2010</u>
</b><br/>Hold up wait a minute King of fiction releases novellas, stop all reading! Bump up to the front of your to-read list! Essential reading right now! Beauty of Kindle is that i could start reading instantly on release date.<br/>King sums these stories in his afterward he says<blockquote> " I have tried my best in Full Dark, No Stars to record what people might do, and how they might behave, under certain dire circumstances. The people in these stories are not without hope, but they acknowledge that </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText17737402759439999023" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Best of 2010</u>
</b><br>Hold up wait a minute King of fiction releases novellas, stop all reading! Bump up to the front of your to-read list! Essential reading right now! Beauty of Kindle is that i could start reading instantly on release date.<br>King sums these stories in his afterward he says<blockquote> " I have tried my best in Full Dark, No Stars to record what people might do, and how they might behave, under certain dire circumstances. The people in these stories are not without hope, but they acknowledge that even our fondest hopes (and our fondest wishes for our fellowmen and the society in which we live) may sometimes be vain. Often, even. But I think they also say that nobility most fully resides not in success but in trying to do the right thing . . "</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>1922</u>
</b><br>King's first novella is a treat of a story, a family who live on a farm with their fates in Kings hand to twist. A story of the darkness of the soul, the evil of what we do and the consequences of our actions. To what extent would you go to preserve the way things exist instead of moving to the big city?<br>The novella starts with this statment.<blockquote>"My name is Wilfred Leland James, and this is my confession. In June of 1922 I murdered my wife, Arlette Christina Winters James, and hid her body by tipping it down an old well."</blockquote>also some more good excerpts..<br><blockquote>"Here is something I learned in 1922: there are always worse things waiting. You think you have seen the most terrible thing, the one that coalesces all your nightmares into a freakish horror that actually exists, and the only consolation is that there can be nothing worse. Even if there is, your mind will snap at the sight of it, and you will know no more. But there is worse, your mind does not snap, and somehow you carry on. You might understand that all the joy has gone... "<br><br>" The Conniving Man out-connived: how do you like that?"</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>Big Driver</u>
</b><br>This story has themes of redemption and atonement. A mystery writer finds herself caught up in her own real life investigation. This story touches you with warmth and compassion for victims of rape and how hard it is for victim to report the crime, the idea of people finding out you have been raped is frightening as the crime. It makes you think about taking the wrong turn being in wrong place at the wrong time. <br><blockquote>The National Crime Victimization Survey says, because I googled it. Sixty percent of rapes go unreported, according to them. Three in every five. I think that might be low, but who can say for sure?"<br> " . . . what she says once in every book: murderers always overlook the obvious."</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>Fair Extension</u>
</b><br>This is the shorter of the four stories its about a twist of fates fortunate become unfortunate and vice versa.<br><blockquote>I was thinking about the Goodhughs. I’ve never known a family to have such a run of bad luck. Bad luck?’ She laughed. ‘Black luck is more like it.’ ”<br>“ ‘Life is fair. We all get the same nine-month shake in the box, and then the dice roll. Some people get a run of sevens. Some people, unfortunately, get snake-eyes. It’s just how the world is.’</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>A Good Marriage</u>
</b><br>This was a gripping story, it made you think, do you really know what your partners up to? If you found out how would you deal with it? The kids, the press, lives could be destroyed.<br><blockquote>He loved nothing, least of all her. Every kindness, caress, boyish grin, and thoughtful gesture – all were nothing but camouflage. He was a shell. There was nothing inside but howling emptiness. ”<br>"She dreamed of going into the dining room and finding a woman bound with chains to the long Ethan Allen table there. The woman was naked except for a black leather hood that covered the top half of her face. I don’t know that woman, that woman is a stranger to me, she thought in her dream, and then from beneath the hood Petra said: ‘Mama, is that you?"<br>"It’s a mistake, it has to be, we’ve been married over half our lives, I’d know, I would know. Opening the box. Thinking, Does anybody really know ”<br>"A marriage was like a house under constant construction, each year seeing the completion of new rooms. A first-year marriage was a cottage; one that had gone on for twenty-seven years was a huge and rambling mansion. There were bound to be crannies and storage spaces, most of them dusty and abandoned, some containing a few unpleasant relics you would just as soon you hadn’t found. But that was no biggie. You either threw those relics out or took them to Goodwill. ”<br>“It’s what drug addicts say. ‘I’ll never take any of that stuff again. I’ve quit before and this time I’ll quit for good. I mean it.’ But they don’t mean it, even when they think they do they don’t, and neither does he. ”<br>"The refrigerator whirred, the water dripped in the sink, and the raw seconds passed. This was the Darker Life, where every truth was written backward."</blockquote><br>Stephen King and his British Fantasy Award for Best Collection.<br><a href="http://s1184.photobucket.com/albums/z322/LouPendergrast/Snapbucket/?action=view&amp;current=417B3A6D.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380341260i/697471._SX540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://s1184.photobucket.com/albums/z322/LouPendergrast/?action=view&amp;current=stokeraward-thumb-250x381-15208-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_2458060052" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2458060052" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32799998-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469767858p2/32799998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2458060052?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/32799998-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32799998-erin?shelf=king-me">king-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32799998-erin?shelf=july-2018">july-2018</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2458060052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3628439916088608116">4.5 Stars<br/><br/>I've somehow stumbled into a Stephen King binge. Its been a long time since I've read Mr. King but I now appear to be back in. <br/><br/>Full Dark, No Stars is a collection of short stories each one in my opinion darker than the last. In my humble opinion no author does the short story collection better than Stephen King and this collection is just further proof of that. <br/><br/>Without spoiling anything I will now give a mini review of each story. <br/><br/>1922 -- 3 Stars<br/>1922 is the first story in this collectio</span>
  <span id="freeText3628439916088608116" style="display:none">4.5 Stars<br /><br />I've somehow stumbled into a Stephen King binge. Its been a long time since I've read Mr. King but I now appear to be back in. <br /><br />Full Dark, No Stars is a collection of short stories each one in my opinion darker than the last. In my humble opinion no author does the short story collection better than Stephen King and this collection is just further proof of that. <br /><br />Without spoiling anything I will now give a mini review of each story. <br /><br />1922 -- 3 Stars<br />1922 is the first story in this collection and the only one to give me an actual nightmare. I will give you a warning if you like me HATE HATE HATE rats maybe skip 1922 I felt sick after reading it. In 1922 we meet a man who suffers some major consequences after the untimely death of his wife. <br /><br />Big Driver --3.5 Stars<br />Big Driver is story #2 all I'll say about this one is a certain evil truck driver fucked with the wrong woman.<br /><br />Fair Extension--4.5 Stars<br />Fair Extension is a strange little story that in some ways reminded me of Thinner. In Fair Extension we meet a man battling terminal cancer who gets quite the deal from a roadside businessman. <br /><br />A Good Marriage--5 Stars<br />A Good Marriage was my absolute favorite story of the bunch. In A Good Marriage a wife learns that the old adage "If you go looking for trouble, you'll find it" is very true. <br /><br />Full Dark, No Stars was very dark and at times I felt very unsettled reading it but if you like Stephen King and aren't afraid of letting a little darkness in I suggest you consider picking this one up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3628439916088608116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3579316623" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3579316623" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3579316623?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3579316623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8730057168887364601">I've been somewhat disenchanted with King as of late, now that I've been going back and re-reading some of his books. His more recent books seem to just be recycling his old material, getting self-indulgent and repetitive, but after reading <i>Full Dark, No Stars</i>, I think he's still got the power as a brilliant contemporary horror writer. This book drops his latest fascination with convoluted character arcs and politics, hearkening back to his older writing, very much scenery-driven, character-driv</span>
  <span id="freeText8730057168887364601" style="display:none">I've been somewhat disenchanted with King as of late, now that I've been going back and re-reading some of his books. His more recent books seem to just be recycling his old material, getting self-indulgent and repetitive, but after reading <i>Full Dark, No Stars</i>, I think he's still got the power as a brilliant contemporary horror writer. This book drops his latest fascination with convoluted character arcs and politics, hearkening back to his older writing, very much scenery-driven, character-driven and timeless, crossing different settings and time periods and presenting some truly interesting stories with a psychological element to them.<br /><br />Prior to reading <i>Full Dark, No Stars</i>, I had already read its most well-known story, <i>1922</i>, and I loved it just as much the second time around. King artfully uses rural isolation, pest animals and tenuous character relationships to create a very chilling, unforgettable tale. <i>Big Driver</i>, also adapted into a film by the same name, wasn't as much of a favourite of mine, but it explores the damage of trauma and what it does to people in a really vivid way. <i>A Good Marriage</i>, like <i>1922</i>, explores two strangers living in the same house and the dynamics of a relationship built from necessity rather than love. I enjoyed it, although the ending was a little weird. Finally there's <i>Fair Extension</i> wherein a man makes a Faustian bargain with the Devil, with unexpected surprises. Not a particularly new or innovative concept, but King brings a good balance of humour and horror together in this one.<br /><br />While the stories aren't perfect, I can definitely say that I really liked each and every one of them. <i>Full Dark, No Stars</i> is a call back to the short story anthologies that readers fell in love with back in the 1980's, and it's great to see that King's still got some tricks up his sleeve and some powerful ideas to work with. Readers who enjoyed <i>Night Shift</i>, <i>Skeleton Crew</i> and <i>Everything's Eventual</i> will really love this one, and the stories are a good mix of different themes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8730057168887364601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_98477878" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98477878" />
    <a title="Kathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/681853-kathy"><img alt="Kathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1201386524p2/681853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98477878?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy" href="/user/show/681853-kathy">Kathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/681853-kathy?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/681853-kathy?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98477878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3260248613036886227">Ok, I am going to review each story, as well, individually as they deserver. <br/><br/>POSSIBLE SPOILERS<br/><br/>1. 1922 - This story is actually a confession of a man who has just murdered his wife. He has even dragged his innocent 14 year old son into this as well, which is very heartbreaking. I feel this story makes you realize that our actions have consequences that we will somehow at some point feel. Is it karma? What goes around, comes around? Ghosts? Insanity? This man, after committing this heinous crime f</span>
  <span id="freeText3260248613036886227" style="display:none">Ok, I am going to review each story, as well, individually as they deserver. <br /><br />POSSIBLE SPOILERS<br /><br />1. 1922 - This story is actually a confession of a man who has just murdered his wife. He has even dragged his innocent 14 year old son into this as well, which is very heartbreaking. I feel this story makes you realize that our actions have consequences that we will somehow at some point feel. Is it karma? What goes around, comes around? Ghosts? Insanity? This man, after committing this heinous crime feels the repercussions in everything breaking down around him. Is he losing his mind? Is he being haunted by his wife? This story in many ways reminds me of King's short story Morality (included w/ Blockade Billy), where one action of a woman completely alter the rest of her life. (5 stars)<br /><br />2. Big Driver - Now this story was very unlike what I know of Uncle Stevie! That being said, I loved it! This is the story of Tessa, a well-known mystery writer who is on her way from a speaking engagement when she is viciously attacked, raped and left for dead. That's horrible enough, right? But this story follows her in how she handles this life-changing situation. This story is incredibly moving and she is an amazingly strong, resilient woman....much to her own surprise. I could not put this story down at all! (5 stars)<br /><br />3. Fair Extension - This book left me a bit torn. Dave Streeter is your average family man with a wife and kids. Dave, however, is dying of cancer and is slowly watching his body deteriorate and his life crumble around him. He comes upon an odd, pudgy little man named George Elvid sitting on the side of the road looking like someone peddling his wares.....however there were no wares. He sells extensions......even a hair extension if that's what Dave wants. But what does Dave want? And what is the cost? <br /><br />This was very well done, who would expect anything less from Uncle Stevie? lol. But I felt left wanting like the story wasn't finished. Or was it? Maybe the rest is for us to think about......was this right or wrong? Maybe too much information wouldn't let us work this one out in our head more. It definitely leaves me w/ alot of questions. (4 stars)<br /><br />4. A Good Marriage - This story was about a woman named Darcy Anderson, who has a pretty charmed life....the good husband and 2 beautiful children. Her husband by all appearances is a mild-mannered accountant, and even volunteers for the boy scouts. They have been married fo 27 years and she thought she knew him pretty well, until she uncovered a secret hiding place of his in the garage. He has a secret that will change everything! <br /><br />This story follows Darcy's discovery and how she handles the nightmare that her life becomes. I really liked this story and respected Darcy very much. (5 stars)<br /><br />**UPDATE**<br />Ok, now with the release of the paperback book, also came the addition of an previously unpublished short story called Under The Weather. All I can say is OMG! I had no idea where this story was going and then all of a sudden I was like "You're $#!@$#! kidding me!" Yup, it's that kind of punchline! This one is possibly one of the best stories in the book. Now I don't want to say too much about this little treasure, but it's the story of a man, who is under a lot of stress due to work, recurring nightmares that he can't explain and a sick wife. Read this short little gem....you'll be glad you did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3260248613036886227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1113632408" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15691735130972746265">This is such a brilliant collection of novellas! It’s my second time around reading it and I enjoyed it even more this time around. The stories in this collection are just so dark and gripping, it’s definitely not a lighthearted read. It explores heavy topics and doesn’t hold back and that’s exactly what I love about King, he isn’t afraid to explore difficult topics!   <span id="freeText15691735130972746265" style="display:none">This is such a brilliant collection of novellas! It’s my second time around reading it and I enjoyed it even more this time around. The stories in this collection are just so dark and gripping, it’s definitely not a lighthearted read. It explores heavy topics and doesn’t hold back and that’s exactly what I love about King, he isn’t afraid to explore difficult topics! My favourite out of the collection is most definitely Big Driver, it just punched me right in the gut and made me feel such a range of emotions. But that isn’t to say I didn’t absolutely love the other stories as well. Each story truly left its mark on me in different ways, this really is a phenomenal collection of novellas!</span>

<div id="review_229428976" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229428976" />
    <a title="Bill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/810550-bill"><img alt="Bill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462234651p2/810550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229428976?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill" href="/user/show/810550-bill">Bill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/810550-bill?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/810550-bill?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229428976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9914758088151465603">Thanks to Goodreads, I have been introduced to a lot of fine authors I<br/>would not otherwise have heard of. Some have become new favorites.<br/>But no matter how enjoyable these authors' works are, none of them can<br/>compare to the security and enjoyment of going back to Stephen King.<br/>I often complain of being a relatively slow reader. But this is never the case with King. He has the wonderful gift of emotionally involving you into a story, coming to know and understand his characters, and when this happens</span>
  <span id="freeText9914758088151465603" style="display:none">Thanks to Goodreads, I have been introduced to a lot of fine authors I<br />would not otherwise have heard of. Some have become new favorites.<br />But no matter how enjoyable these authors' works are, none of them can<br />compare to the security and enjoyment of going back to Stephen King.<br />I often complain of being a relatively slow reader. But this is never the case with King. He has the wonderful gift of emotionally involving you into a story, coming to know and understand his characters, and when this happens, the mechanics of reading disappear. It becomes an immersion.<br /><br />In King's afterword (and I love that he does these), he explains exactly why his storytelling resonates with me perfectly:<br /><br />"for those who substitute unbelievable behavior for the way people really act, I have nothing but contempt. Bad writing is more than a matter of shit syntax and faulty observation; bad writing usually arises from a stubborn refusal to tell stories about what people actually do."<br /><br />He may sound snarky out of context, but he's right. Personally, there<br />is no way I can thoroughly enjoy a story if the characters' actions make no sense.<br /><br />I have tried to explain this in a couple of reviews I have written for two novels by a very popular horror writer here. I'm not going to mention his name, but the reason I don't care for his stories is because I feel that his main characters are idiots. Despite his talent for laying out a story, it was ruined for me because I didn't buy in to what the characters did, or their motivations.<br />King gets it. (Okay, except for Under the Dome. I couldn't buy into where human nature went in that one, sorry Steve, we're off the common plane there, old friend.) <br /><br />With this collection, King returns to his excellent novella formula. Full Dark, No Stars is also a return to humankind's darkness, and also in his afterword, he explains that rather than have extraordinary characters in ordinary situations, he chooses to put ordinary people in extraordinary situations and see what happens. This is a recipe that yields stories that share the addictive quality of, "I can't wait to see how this ends!"<br /><br />So get comfy, sit back and enjoy four tales of harshness...<br /><br />1922: This was a good story set in 1922, where a farmer comes to a final solution regarding his wife's insistence on selling their land off.<br />After about 100 pages, I was beginning to feel that there were parts<br />that dragged a bit, but King wrapped this one up with a high one, left<br />center field, out of the park, off a windshield and into the river.<br />I was left thinking about this one for a while.<br /><br />Big Driver: Oooh, this was a dark one. I think my posture is still suffering from my slack-jawed slouch as King pulled me through the story of a writer of cozy mysteries, and her trip back from a speaking engagement.<br />After showing us his softer side over the past few years, our Stephen shows he still has dark things in the tank. I had a hard time putting this one down.<br /><br />Fair Extension: The shortest story in the book. This one reminded me a little of The Monkey's Paw, in that you may get what you desire, but in the grand balance of things, something must be taken to be given. Again, a tough one to put down.<br /><br />A Good Marriage: After 27 years of marriage, a woman discovers that her<br />loving husband has a secret hobby. It's not good news. I was again hauled through this story mercilessly.<br /><br />Afterword: Probably the most terrifying part of this novel for me was learning that King still goes for his 4-5 mile walks along a road (he was hit by a van in 1999, for those of you who don't know), and that his favorite snack is a candybar and a soda.<br />Firstly, if you ever read this, Steve, please stay off the roads. And knock off the white sugar (aka white death). I want you to stay healthy and keep writing for many more years. Walk in the woods, and eat plenty of Omega-3s, antioxidants and get your fibre. Peace.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9914758088151465603" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
